After the initial\n    44→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    45→// and how it should be processed.\n    46→//\n    47→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    48→//\n    49→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    50→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    51→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    52→//   sent asynchronously.\n    53→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    54→//\n    55→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    56→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    57→// processor must send a matching response.\n    58→//\n    59→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    60→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    61→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    62→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    63→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    64→//   to SEND.\n    65→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    66→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    67→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    68→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    69→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    70→//   request trailers.\n    71→//\n    72→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    73→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    74→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    75→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    76→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    77→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    78→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    79→//\n    80→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    81→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    82→//\n    83→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    84→//   on the content of the headers.\n    85→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    86→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    87→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    88→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    89→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    90→//\n    91→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    92→// server\n    93→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    94→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    95→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    96→//\n    97→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    98→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    99→// name.\n   100→//\n   101→// [#next-free-field: 20]\n   102→message ExternalProcessor {\n   103→  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n   104→  // is received in response to request headers.\n   105→  enum RouteCacheAction {\n   106→    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n   107→    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   108→    // field is set in an external processor response.\n   109→    DEFAULT = 0;\n   110→\n   111→    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   112→    // the external processor response.\n   113→    CLEAR = 1;\n   114→\n   115→    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   116→    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n   117→    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n   118→    // to true.\n   119→    RETAIN = 2;\n   120→  }\n   121→\n   122→  reserved 4;\n   123→\n   124→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   125→\n   126→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   127→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   128→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   129→\n   130→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   131→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   132→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   133→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   134→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   135→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   136→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   137→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   138→\n   139→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   140→  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n   141→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n   142→\n   143→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   144→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   145→  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n   146→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n   147→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   148→  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n   149→\n   150→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   151→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   152→  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n   153→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   154→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   155→  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n   156→\n   157→  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n   158→  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n   159→  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n   160→  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n   161→  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n   162→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   163→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   164→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   165→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   166→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   167→    gte {}\n   168→  }];\n   169→\n   170→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n   171→  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n   172→  string stat_prefix = 8;\n   173→\n   174→  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n   175→  // make to message headers. The metadata\n   200→  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n   201→  // ext_proc filter name.\n   202→  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n   203→\n   204→  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n   205→  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n   206→  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n   207→  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n   208→  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n   209→  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n   210→\n   211→  // If set to true, ignore the\n   212→  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n   213→  // message in an external processor response. ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 20]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n    // field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. A set of\n    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n  }\n}\n\n// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n// [#next-free-field: 8]\nmessage ExtProcOverrides {\n  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n  bool async_mode = 2;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n\n  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n  // config used. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_015bCr6K7bwyqKXCx4rvjL2v","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→syntax = \"proto3\";\n     2→\n     3→package   16→\n    17→option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n    18→option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n    19→option java_multiple_files = true;\n    20→option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n    21→option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n    22→\n    23→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    24→// External Processing Filter\n    25→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    26→\n    27→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    28→\n    29→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    30→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    31→//\n    32→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    33→\n    34→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    35→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    36→//\n    37→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    39→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    40→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    41→//\n    42→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    43→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    44→// and how it should be processed.\n    45→//\n    46→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    47→//\n    48→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    49→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    50→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    51→//   sent asynchronously.\n    52→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    53→//\n    54→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    55→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    56→// processor must send a matching response.\n    57→//\n    58→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    59→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    60→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    61→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    62→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    63→//   to SEND.\n    64→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    65→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    66→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    67→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    68→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    69→//   request trailers.\n    70→//\n    71→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    72→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    73→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    74→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    75→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    76→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    77→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    78→//\n    79→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    80→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    81→//\n    82→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    83→//   on the content of the headers.\n    84→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    85→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    86→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    87→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    88→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    89→//\n    90→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    91→// server\n    92→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    93→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    94→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    95→//\n    96→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    97→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    98→// name.\n    99→//\n   100→// [#next-free-field: 18]\n   101→message ExternalProcessor {\n   102→  reserved 4;\n   103→\n   104→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   105→\n   106→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   107→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   108→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   109→\n   110→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   111→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   112→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   113→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   114→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   115→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   116→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   117→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   118→\n   119→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   120→  // sent. = \"proto3\";\n\npackage envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n\nimport \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n\nimport \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\nimport \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\noption java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\noption java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\noption java_multiple_files = true;\noption go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\noption (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 18]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n    // definition for safe parsing.\n    repeated string typed = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n  // the external processing server.\n  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n}\n\n// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n//\n// This works as below:\n//\n//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n//   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   3. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_011ALWdKAgQSq1FFFrv9kx9b","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→.. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n     2→\n     3→External Processing\n     4→===================\n     5→* This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n     6→* :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n     7→\n     8→The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n     9→to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n    10→it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n    11→and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n    12→\n    13→The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    14→external processor\n    15→:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    16→messages, and the processor must reply with\n    17→:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n    18→messages.\n    19→\n    20→Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n    21→This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n    22→request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n    23→on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n    24→that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n    25→stream requests from the proxy.\n    26→\n    27→This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n    28→are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n    29→be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n    30→\n    31→Statistics\n    32→----------\n    33→This filter outputs statistics in the\n    34→``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n    35→<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n    36→comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n    37→\n    38→The following statistics are supported:\n    39→\n    40→.. csv-table::\n    41→  :header: Name, Type, Description\n    42→  :widths: auto\n    43→\n    44→  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n    45→  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n    46→  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n    47→  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n    48→  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n    49→  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n    50→  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n    51→  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n    52→  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n    53→  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n    54→  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n    55→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\nit to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\nand modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n\nThe protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\nexternal processor\n:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\nmessages, and the processor must reply with\n:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\nmessages.\n\nConfiguration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\nThis way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\nrequest and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\nbe found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n\nStatistics\n----------\nThis filter outputs statistics in the\n``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01VhCaLhAYqD4r1iHpfHCRxC","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01RuvGCMSH33JZaGy32m3zMH","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide: v1.30 → v1.31\n\n## Overview\n\nThis guide provides comprehensive information for migrating the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0. The upgrade includes:\n\n- **New route cache action configuration** providing more granular control over route cache clearing behavior\n- **Deferred stream closure timeout** for improved observability mode handling\n- **Enhanced observability mode** with better stream lifecycle management\n- **HTTP status code change** for timeout errors (504 instead of 500)\n- **Improved gRPC tracing context propagation**\n\nThe migration involves both configuration changes and behavioral adjustments. While most existing configurations remain backward compatible, new features are available to improve performance and observability.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Clearing Behavior (HIGH PRIORITY)\n\n**What Changed:** The route cache clearing behavior has been refactored from a simple boolean flag to a three-state enum, with changes to the clearing logic.\n\n**Impact Level:** MEDIUM\n\n**Details:**\n\nIn v1.30, route cache clearing was controlled by a single boolean field:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache`: If `true`, prevents clearing the route cache\n\nIn v1.31, this has been replaced by a more flexible enum-based approach:\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  DEFAULT = 0;   // Clear if clear_route_cache is set AND header mutation exists\n  CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear (ignoring the clear_route_cache bit)\n  RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear (equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache = true)\n}\n```\n\n**Key Behavioral Differences:**\n\n| Scenario | v1.30 Behavior | v1.31 Behavior (route_cache_action) |\n|----------|----------------|--------------------------------------|\n| No header mutation | Route cache NOT cleared | Route cache NOT cleared (regardless of `route_cache_action`); `clear_route_cache_ignored` stat incremented |\n| Header mutation + `clear_route_cache=true` + `disable_clear_route_cache=false` | Cache cleared | **Depends on mode:**<br/>- DEFAULT: Cache cleared<br/>- CLEAR: Cache cleared<br/>- RETAIN: NOT cleared |\n| Upstream filter chain | Route cache NOT cleared | Route cache NOT cleared (upstream route cache not clearable) |\n\n**Configuration Examples:**\n\nBefore (v1.30):\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  disable_clear_route_cache: false  # Default behavior\n```\n\nAfter (v1.31) - Equivalent configurations:\n```yaml\n# Option 1: DEFAULT behavior (matches v1.30 behavior)\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n\n# Option 2: Always clear (when mutations occur)\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n\n# Option 3: Never clear (equivalent to v1.30's disable_clear_route_cache=true)\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Backward Compatibility Note:** The field `disable_clear_route_cache` is still supported in v1.31 with a migration annotation. When `disable_clear_route_cache=true` is set, it is automatically converted to `route_cache_action=RETAIN`. However, **you cannot set both fields to non-default values** - this will cause a configuration validation error:\n> \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\"\n\n---\n\n### 2. External Processor Timeout Error Status Code\n\n**What Changed:** Timeout errors from the external processor now return HTTP 504 (Gateway Timeout) instead of HTTP 500 (Internal Server Error).\n\n**Impact Level:** LOW\n\n**Details:**\n\n**v1.30 Behavior:** When a message timeout occurred waiting for a response from the external processor:\n- Return status code: **500 Internal Server Error**\n- Error response was sent to downstream clients\n\n**v1.31 Behavior:** Same timeout condition:\n- Return status code: **504 Gateway Timeout**\n- More semantically correct for upstream service timeouts\n\n**Why This Matters:**\n- Downstream clients may differentiate handling based on status code\n- Monitoring/alerting systems may track 5xx vs 4xx errors differently\n- Load balancers may handle 504 differently than 500 (some don't retry 504s by default)\n\n**Migration Action:**\n- Review downstream client error handling code\n- Update monitoring/alerting rules that count 500 errors\n- Verify load balancer retry policies handle 504 appropriately\n- Test retry behavior with external processor timeouts\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `disable_clear_route_cache` Field (DEPRECATION)\n\n**Deprecation Status:** DEPRECATED (still functional in v1.31, planned for removal in v1.32+)\n\n**Details:**\n\nThe boolean field `disable_clear_route_cache` is now superseded by the `route_cache_action` enum:\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30 & v1.31 (deprecated in v1.31)\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n// v1.31 (new, recommended)\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n```\n\n**Migration Path:**\n\n| Current Configuration | Migration Path |\n|----------------------|----------------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) | Use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` or omit (DEFAULT is the default) |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n| Not set (defaults to false) | No action needed; system defaults to DEFAULT behavior |\n\n**Recommended Timeline:**\n1. **Immediately:** Migrate to `route_cache_action` in new configurations\n2. **Within 1-2 releases:** Update existing configurations to use `route_cache_action`\n3. **Future release:** `disable_clear_route_cache` will be removed\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Enum\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**Purpose:** Provides three distinct strategies for handling route cache clearing in response to external processor responses.\n\n**Configuration Field:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n    CLEAR = 1;\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n\n- **DEFAULT (recommended):** Respects the external processor's `clear_route_cache` flag only when header mutations are present. Best for most use cases where the processor decides when cache clearing is needed.\n\n- **CLEAR:** Always clears the route cache when the external processor responds to request headers. Useful when you want to ensure routes are recalculated after every ext_proc interaction, regardless of the processor's response.\n\n- **RETAIN:** Never clears the route cache, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` requests from the processor. Use when you're confident routes don't change or want to maximize route cache hit rates.\n\n**Configuration Examples:**\n\n```yaml\n# Example 1: DEFAULT mode (recommended)\n- name: ext_proc_default\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n\n# Example 2: CLEAR mode (always refresh routes)\n- name: ext_proc_always_clear\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n\n# Example 3: RETAIN mode (never clear cache)\n- name: ext_proc_never_clear\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n---\n\n### 2. Deferred Stream Closure Timeout\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+\n\n**Purpose:** Controls how long gRPC streams to the external processor remain open after filter destruction in observability mode.\n\n**Configuration Field:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n```\n\n**Default Value:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n\n**Details:**\n\nIn observability mode (`observability_mode: true`), the external processor stream may be kept open independently of the main HTTP request/response stream. This timeout controls how long Envoy will wait before forcefully closing that stream if it hasn't closed gracefully.\n\n**When This Matters:**\n\n- **Observability mode enabled:** The external processor receives messages asynchronously and may process them after the HTTP response completes\n- **Filter destruction:** When the filter is destroyed (request complete), instead of immediately closing the stream, it defers the closure\n- **Timeout:** If the stream doesn't close naturally within `deferred_close_timeout`, Envoy forcefully terminates it\n\n**Configuration Examples:**\n\n```yaml\n# Example 1: Default timeout (5 seconds)\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Optional, this is the default\n\n# Example 2: Shorter timeout (1 second) for faster cleanup\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 1s\n\n# Example 3: Longer timeout (10 seconds) to allow more processing time\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s\n```\n\n**Performance Implications:**\n\n- **Too short:** External processor may not complete processing; stream closed prematurely\n- **Too long:** More memory/connection overhead; slower resource cleanup\n- **Optimal:** Choose based on typical external processor response time\n\n**Related to Observability Mode:**\n\nThe `deferred_close_timeout` is specifically for the async/deferred handling in observability mode:\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true  # Enable \"Send and Go\" mode\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Control cleanup timing\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\nIn observability mode:\n1. Envoy sends messages to the external processor without waiting for responses\n2. The processor observes data but responses are ignored\n3. When the HTTP stream ends, the ext_proc stream is marked for deferred closure\n4. After `deferred_close_timeout` expires, the stream is forcefully closed\n\n---\n\n### 3. Enhanced Observability Mode\n\n**Availability:** v1.31.0+ (improved from v1.30)\n\n**Enhancements:**\n\n1. **Better Stream Lifecycle Management:** Streams are now managed by a thread-local stream manager, preventing premature closure while the external processor is still processing\n\n2. **Deferred Closure:** Streams remain open for a configured duration after the HTTP request completes, allowing the external processor to complete its work\n\n3. **Flow Control Support:** Added support for gRPC side-stream flow control with watermark callbacks\n\n4. **Safer Async Processing:** Improved handling of filter destruction timing to prevent use-after-free bugs\n\n**Configuration:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Key Points:**\n\n- The external processor should **not** send response messages; they are ignored\n- Only STREAMED and NONE body processing modes are supported\n- Flow control is now available to prevent overwhelming the processor\n- Deferred closure ensures graceful stream cleanup\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Step 1: Identify Current Usage of `disable_clear_route_cache`\n\nSearch your Envoy configurations for any use of `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n```bash\n# Find all ext_proc configurations with disable_clear_route_cache\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/configs/\n```\n\n### Step 2: Update Route Cache Configuration\n\nFor each configuration using `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n**If `disable_clear_route_cache: false` or omitted (default):**\n```yaml\n# Old\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: false\n\n# New (explicit, recommended)\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**If `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:**\n```yaml\n# Old\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# New\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### Step 3: Consider Using CLEAR Mode if Applicable\n\nIf you want to ensure routes are always refreshed after ext_proc processing:\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n```\n\n### Step 4: Configure Deferred Close Timeout (if using observability_mode)\n\nIf observability mode is enabled, explicitly set the deferred close timeout based on your workload:\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Adjust based on processor response time\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n```\n\n### Step 5: Test Error Handling for 504 Responses\n\nUpdate any downstream error handling code that specifically catches or handles 500 errors from ext_proc timeouts:\n\n```python\n# Example: If you had code like this\ntry:\n    response = requests.get(envoy_url)\nexcept requests.HTTPError as e:\n    if e.response.status_code == 500:\n        # Might have been an ext_proc timeout\n        # Now it will be 504 instead\nexcept requests.HTTPError as e:\n    if e.response.status_code == 504:\n        # This is now the ext_proc timeout code\n```\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Route Cache Clearing Logic\n\n**v1.30 Logic:**\n```\nif clear_route_cache AND NOT disable_clear_route_cache:\n    clear_route_cache()\nelse:\n    do_nothing()\n```\n\n**v1.31 Logic:**\n```\nif no header mutation:\n    do_nothing()  # No reason to clear\nelse:\n    switch route_cache_action:\n        case DEFAULT:\n            if clear_route_cache:\n                clear_route_cache()\n        case CLEAR:\n            clear_route_cache()  # Always\n        case RETAIN:\n            do_nothing()  # Never\n```\n\n**Key Difference:** v1.31 adds a check for header mutations, preventing unnecessary cache clearing when headers aren't modified.\n\n**Impact:**\n- Fewer unnecessary route cache clears\n- Better performance in scenarios with many header-only requests\n- More explicit control through `route_cache_action` enum\n\n### 2. Stream Management in Observability Mode\n\n**v1.30:**\n- Streams closed immediately on filter destruction\n- Risk of message loss if processor still processing\n- No flow control support\n\n**v1.31:**\n- Streams deferred closure via thread-local manager\n- Processor gets `deferred_close_timeout` to finish\n- Flow control supported via watermark callbacks\n- Safer async handling\n\n### 3. Error Response Status Code\n\n**v1.30:**\n- Timeout → **500 Internal Server Error**\n- May mislead about error source\n\n**v1.31:**\n- Timeout → **504 Gateway Timeout**\n- More accurate semantic for upstream timeouts\n- Clearer for monitoring/alerting\n\n### 4. Tracing Context Propagation\n\n**v1.30:**\n- Tracing context headers not always propagated to ext_proc\n\n**v1.31:**\n- Tracing context headers consistently propagated in bidirectional streams\n- Better distributed tracing support\n- Improved observability\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Phase 1: Preparation (Pre-Upgrade)\n\n1. **Audit Current Configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"ext_proc\\|external_processor\" /path/to/configs/ | grep -E \"yml|yaml\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Document Current Behavior:**\n   - Note which ext_proc filters use `disable_clear_route_cache`\n   - Record current route cache hit rates if monitored\n   - Document timeout error handling code\n\n3. **Test Timeout Error Handling:**\n   - Simulate ext_proc service timeouts\n   - Verify downstream services handle 500 errors\n   - Plan for 504 response handling\n\n### Phase 2: Configuration Update (Upgrade Compatible)\n\n1. **Update Configurations to Use `route_cache_action`:**\n   ```yaml\n   # For each ext_proc filter\n   ext_proc:\n     # Remove: disable_clear_route_cache: true/false\n     # Add one of:\n     route_cache_action: DEFAULT    # Recommended\n     # OR\n     route_cache_action: CLEAR      # If always clearing\n     # OR\n     route_cache_action: RETAIN     # If never clearing\n   ```\n\n2. **If Using Observability Mode, Set Deferred Timeout:**\n   ```yaml\n   ext_proc:\n     observability_mode: true\n     deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Adjust to your needs\n   ```\n\n3. **Validate Configurations:**\n   ```bash\n   envoy -c /path/to/config.yaml --mode validate-only\n   ```\n\n### Phase 3: Testing (Before Production Deployment)\n\n1. **Unit/Integration Tests:**\n   - Test ext_proc with various `route_cache_action` settings\n   - Verify header mutation detection\n   - Test timeout scenarios\n\n2. **Performance Testing:**\n   - Route cache hit rates with DEFAULT vs CLEAR\n   - Stream cleanup timing with various `deferred_close_timeout` values\n   - Memory usage in observability mode\n\n3. **Error Handling Tests:**\n   - Timeout responses (verify 504 status code)\n   - Downstream client behavior with 504 vs 500\n   - Monitoring/alerting rule accuracy\n\n### Phase 4: Staging Deployment\n\n1. **Canary Deployment:**\n   - Deploy v1.31 to small percentage of traffic\n   - Monitor error rates and latency\n   - Watch for 504 errors from ext_proc timeouts\n\n2. **Configuration Validation:**\n   - Verify all ext_proc filters use `route_cache_action`\n   - Confirm deferred close timeout works correctly\n   - Test observability mode if enabled\n\n3. **Rollback Plan:**\n   - Revert to v1.30 if critical issues found\n   - Have configuration rollback prepared\n\n### Phase 5: Production Deployment\n\n1. **Gradual Rollout:**\n   - Start with low traffic percentage\n   - Gradually increase based on metrics\n   - Monitor for issues\n\n2. **Monitoring:**\n   - Track `clear_route_cache_*` stats changes\n   - Watch for 504 errors\n   - Monitor route cache hit rates\n\n3. **Post-Deployment Verification:**\n   - Confirm expected route cache behavior\n   - Validate error handling works\n   - Review performance metrics\n\n### Phase 6: Cleanup (Post-Deployment)\n\n1. **Remove Old Comments:**\n   - Update documentation to reflect v1.31\n   - Remove references to `disable_clear_route_cache`\n\n2. **Optimize Configuration:**\n   - Fine-tune `route_cache_action` based on metrics\n   - Adjust `deferred_close_timeout` if needed\n\n3. **Plan Future Deprecation:**\n   - Mark calendar for removal of `disable_clear_route_cache` support\n   - Plan removal of `async_mode` (being replaced by `observability_mode`)\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Unit Tests\n\n**Route Cache Behavior:**\n```python\n# Test DEFAULT mode with header mutation\nconfig.route_cache_action = DEFAULT\nconfig.disable_clear_route_cache = False\nresponse.clear_route_cache = True\nheaders_mutated = True\nassert route_cache_cleared() == True\n\n# Test DEFAULT mode without header mutation\nconfig.route_cache_action = DEFAULT\nresponse.clear_route_cache = True\nheaders_mutated = False\nassert route_cache_cleared() == False\n\n# Test CLEAR mode always clears\nconfig.route_cache_action = CLEAR\nresponse.clear_route_cache = False\nheaders_mutated = True\nassert route_cache_cleared() == True\n\n# Test RETAIN mode never clears\nconfig.route_cache_action = RETAIN\nresponse.clear_route_cache = True\nheaders_mutated = True\nassert route_cache_cleared() == False\n```\n\n**Status Code for Timeouts:**\n```python\n# Simulate ext_proc timeout\next_proc_service.delay = 10 * timeout\nresponse = send_request()\nassert response.status_code == 504  # v1.31 change\n# (v1.30 would return 500)\n```\n\n### 2. Performance Tests\n\n**Route Cache Hit Rates:**\n```\nMetric: Route cache hit ratio\nBefore: baseline\nAfter (DEFAULT): should be same or better\nAfter (CLEAR): likely lower\nAfter (RETAIN): likely higher (but may be incorrect)\n```\n\n**Stream Lifecycle:**\n```\nMetric: Memory usage per stream\nObservability mode with deferred closure:\n- Peak memory: ~same (stream still held)\n- Peak duration: longer (deferred wait)\n- Cleanup: cleaner (less premature closure)\n```\n\n**Error Handling Latency:**\n```\nMetric: Time to return 504 error\nShould be similar to previous 500 error time\n(Just different status code, same timeout)\n```\n\n### 4. Load Testing\n\n**Concurrent Streams in Observability Mode:**\n```\nConfig:\n- observability_mode: true\n- deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n\nLoad: 1000 concurrent requests\nMeasure:\n- Peak connection count (should be manageable)\n- Memory growth over time (should be bounded)\n- Stream closure rate (should be steady)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If Issues Occur After Upgrade\n\n**Immediate Rollback (0-5 minutes):**\n1. Revert Envoy to v1.30.0\n2. Keep old configuration (both formats supported)\n3. Monitor metrics to verify behavior\n\n**Configuration Rollback (if needed):**\n```yaml\n# If v1.31 config doesn't work\n# Revert to v1.30 style\n\n# Change this:\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n\n# Back to this:\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: false\n```\n\n### Troubleshooting Common Issues\n\n**Issue: Configuration validation fails**\n```\nError: \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action\ncan not be set to none-default at the same time.\"\n\nSolution:\n- Remove disable_clear_route_cache from config\n- Keep only route_cache_action\n```\n\n**Issue: Route cache not clearing as expected**\n```\nProblem: route_cache_action: DEFAULT but cache not cleared\n\nDiagnostic:\n1. Check if headers are being mutated\n2. Check if clear_route_cache flag is set by processor\n3. Check upstream vs downstream filter chain\n\nSolution:\n- Use route_cache_action: CLEAR to force clearing\n- Or verify processor sets clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**Issue: Observability mode streams not closing**\n```\nProblem: gRPC connections to ext_proc staying open too long\n\nSolution:\n1. Reduce deferred_close_timeout value\n2. Verify processor is handling stream closure correctly\n3. Check for processor-side hanging connections\n```\n\n**Issue: 504 errors being handled as 500**\n```\nProblem: Downstream expecting 500 from ext_proc timeout\n\nSolution:\n1. Update error handling code to expect 504\n2. Update monitoring/alerting rules\n3. Verify load balancer doesn't treat 504 specially\n```\n\n---\n\n## Pro Tips for Successful Migration\n\n### 1. Use DEFAULT Mode for Most Cases\nUnless you have specific requirements, use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`:\n- Most compatible with v1.30 behavior\n- Respects processor decisions\n- Good performance\n\n### 4. use `observability_mode` |\n\n---\n\n## Reference\n\n### Proto Messages\n\n**New Enum (v1.31):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // DEFAULT: Clear cache only if processor sets clear_route_cache AND headers mutated\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // CLEAR: Always clear cache (ignore processor's clear_route_cache flag)\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // RETAIN: Never clear cache (ignore processor's clear_route_cache flag)\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**New Field (v1.31):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n\n  // Timeout for deferred stream closure in observability mode.\n  // Default: 5000 milliseconds\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n```\n\n**Deprecated Field (still present in v1.31):**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // DEPRECATED: Use route_cache_action instead\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n### Related Files\n\n**Proto Definitions:**\n- `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Implementation:**\n- `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n- `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`\n- `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc`\n- `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.cc`\n\n**Documentation:**\n- `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`\n\n### Key Statistics\n\n**New stats (v1.31):** None new\n\n**Updated stats (v1.31):**\n- `clear_route_cache_ignored`: Now incremented when no header mutation detected\n- `clear_route_cache_disabled`: Now incremented when `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n\n---\n\n## Support and Questions\n\nFor additional help with the migration:\n1.
